2.3. Misc

  • S. K. Saxena, Hindustani Sangeet and a Philosopher of Art: Music, Rhythm, and Kathak Dance Vis-à-vis Aesthetics of Susanne K. Langer. D.K. Printworld, 2001.

3. STEMM

3.1. Science

  • B. C. Deva, The Music Of India: A Scientific Study. Munshiram Manoharlal, 1981.
  • G. H. Ranade, Hindusthāni Music: An Outline Of Its Physics And Aesthetics. Sangli: G.H. Ranade, 1938.
    • Dated, but really nice, easy for understanding some aspects of the theory of Hindustani Classical Music.
  • S. Rao, Acoustical Perspective On Raga-Rasa Theory., Munshiram Manoharlal Publishers, 2000.
  • A. K. Datta, R. Sengupta, K. Banerjee, and D. Ghosh, Acoustical Analysis of the Tanpura: Indian Plucked String Instrument. Springer, 2018.
  • A. K. Datta, S. S. Solanki, R. Sengupta, S. Chakraborty, K. Mahto, and A. Patranabis, Signal Analysis of Hindustani Classical Music. Springer, 2017.
  • S. Chakraborty, G. Mazzola, S. Tewari, and M. Patra, Computational Musicology in Hindustani Music. Springer, 2014.

3.2. Tech

  • A. Deb, “Technology continues to challenge Hindustani music in productive ways,” The Caravan. https://caravanmagazine.in/perspectives/record-2 (accessed Jan. 22, 2022).

    3. ICM Recordings: Some Non Introductory Pieces
      • Function/Mappings
        • Rasa
          • General
            • “Rasa (aesthetics),” Wikipedia. Mar. 10, 2022. Accessed: Mar. 19, 2022. [Online]. Available: https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rasa_(aesthetics)&oldid=1076290549
              • Śṛṅgāraḥ (शृङ्गारः): Romance, Love, Attractiveness. Presiding Deity: Vishnu. Colour: Light Green
              • Hāsyam (हास्यं): Laughter, Mirth, Comedy. Presiding Deity: Shiva. Colour: White
              • Raudram (रौद्रं): Fury. Presiding Deity: Shiva. Colour: Red
              • Kāruṇyam (कारुण्यं): Compassion, Mercy. Presiding Deity: Yama. Colour: Grey
              • Bībhatsam (बीभत्सं): Disgust, Aversion. Presiding Deity: Shiva. Colour: Blue
              • Bhayānakam (भयानकं): Horror, Terror. Presiding Deity: Yama. Colour: Black
              • Veeram (वीरं): Heroism. Presiding Deity: Indra. Colour: Saffron
              • Adbhutam (अद्भुतं): Wonder, Amazement. Presiding Deity: Brahma. Colour: Yellow
              • Śāntam: Peace Or Tranquility. Presiding Deity: Vishnu. Colour: Perpetual White.
          • Shringar
            • General
              • Śṛṅgāraḥ (शृङ्गारः): Romance, Love, attractiveness. Presiding deity: Vishnu. Colour: light green

5.1.9. Misc

5.2. Theory

5.2.1. General

  • V. P. Singha And S. Benegal, An Introduction To Hindustani Classical Music: A Guidebook For Beginners. Roli Books, 2014.
  • “Home,” Rajan Parrikar Music Archive. Accessed: Nov. 18, 2024. [Online]. Available: https://www.parrikar.org/
    • Rajan Parrikar Music Archive
      • A highly opinionated, 'inclusive' (as in, you'll often find likes of Lata Mangeshkar, Dagar bandhu on the very same page) web resource on Indian Classical Music. Novice students, and listeners past filmy, 'Music of the X' series sort of stages and transitioning into unadulterated raagdaari sangeet, will find it particularly useful.
  • R. R. Menon: Excellent introductory (but not necessarily the best first) books on Indian Classical Music for everyone.
    • R. R. Menon, Indian Classical Music: An Initiation. New Delhi: Vision Books, 1997.
    • R. R. Menon, Indian Music: The Magic Of The Raga. Somaiya Publications, 1998.
    • R. R. Menon, Penguin Dictionary of Indian Classical Music, First Edition. New Delhi, India ; New York, NY, USA: Penguin, 1995.

5.2.2. Dictionaries

  • P. Amarnath, The Dictionary of Hindustani Classical Music. Viking, 2020.

5.2.3. Reference Works

  • V. Bhatkhande, Hindustani Sangeet Paddhati Kramik Pustak Maalika. Sangeet Karyalay, 2017.

5.2.4. Core

  1. Core Components
    1. Time
      • Texts
        • M. Clayton, Time in Indian Music: Rhythm, Metre, and Form in North Indian Rag Performance. Oxford University Press, 2008.
        • G. M. Wegner, Vintage Tabla Repertory: Drum Composition of North Indian Classical Music, Har/Com edition. New Delhi: Munshiram Manoharlal Publishers, 2006.
        • R. S. Gottlieb, Solo Tabla Drumming of North India: Its Repertoire, Styles and Performance Practices, Pap/Cas edition. Delhi: Motilal Banarsidass Publishers, 1998.
      • Videos
        • “Manjul BHARGAVA - Poetry, Drumming and Mathematics - YouTube.” Accessed: Dec. 17, 2024. [Online]. Available: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0LraLjkvgGo
      • Misc
    2. Tonal X
      • Compositional Forms
        • V. Chandorkar, Compositional Forms of Hindustani Music: A Journey. Munshiram Manoharlal Publishers, 2012.
      • Ragas
        • N. A. Jairazbhoy, The Rāgs Of North Indian Music: Their Structure And Evolution. Popular Prakashan, 1995.
        • J. Bor, The Raga Guide: A Survey of 74 Hindustani Ragas. Nimbus Records, 1992.
        • P. Moutal, Hindustānī Rāga-s Index: Bibliographical References on Descriptions, Compositions, and Vistāra-s of Hindustānī Rāga-s Based on Selected Major Contemporary Works in Devanāgarī. Munshiram Manoharlal Publishers, 1991.
    3. Language
      • S. Mudgal, A. Pradhan, and K. Ray, Shabd Aur Sangeet: Unravelling Song-text in India. Three Essays Collective, 2019.
      • J. L. Martinez, Semiosis in Hindustani Music. Motilal Banarsidass Publ., 2001.
      • F. Orsini and K. B. Schofield, Eds., Tellings and Texts: Music, Literature and Performance in North India. 2015.
  2. Medium X
    1. Vocal Music
      • I. Srivastava, A Practical Guide To North Indian Classical Vocal Music: The Ten Basic Of Rā.Gs With Compositions And Improvisations., Munshiram Manoharlal Publishers, 2008.
    2. Instrumental Music
      • G. Ruckert and A. A. Khan, The Classical Music of North India: The First Years Study. Munshiram Manoharlal Publishers, 1998.
        • A nice reference for novice sarod players.
